## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (driving force). The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force, damping, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (harmonic driving)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 - x**2) (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Quadratic-cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (c1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (mixed nonlinear terms)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (combined friction models)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well; even powers (x²) → asymmetric potential
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v indicate energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping switching (self-sustained oscillations, limit cycles)
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates externally driven oscillation
- Products x*v or x²*v suggest nonlinear coupling between position and velocity (non-conservative forces)
- Cubic restoring force x³ with same/opposite sign as linear term x indicates hardening/softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or has simple dissipation
- Rational forms like v/(1 + c*x²) can model position-dependent damping coefficients
